[476] Sam let Mr. Inperiali leave. As soon as Mr. Inperiali left, Sam's face fell and he shouted, "Collins!"
[477] The tall Irishman reluctantly followed, with his lips drooping unhappily. No matter what Sam asked, he answered impatiently and rudely. Sam grabbed his collar and said, "Listen carefully, you bloodsucking politician," Sam said, "I've been wanting to tell you this for a long time. I know you were playing games with me last night, thinking you could dodge today's questioning, but you can't dodge it, can you? You damn public servant, you said you came here yesterday to confront Longstreth and get an explanation, that you two didn't argue. I didn't want to dig deeper then, but I'm going to get to the bottom of it this morning. Now tell me the truth, the whole truth."
[478] Collins was trembling with anger and pushed Sam's hand away. "You're a smart cop, aren't you?" Collins roared, "Do you think I would kiss him? Of course, I would yell at him – I hope that dirty bastard goes to hell. Damn, it made me bankrupt!"
[479] Sam smiled at Jonas. "Did you write that down, Jonas?" He turned back to Collins. "A good reason to kill him, isn't it?"
[480] Collins sneered maliciously. "Very clever, too clever. I must have prepared that poisoned cork ready to go, waiting for the stock to fall? Think again, Sam, what do you have to be a detective."
[481] Sam raised an eyebrow and continued, "Why didn't DeWitt know anything about Longstreth's suggestion to buy stocks?"
[482] "Why? I'm as curious as you are," Collins said, looking dissatisfied. "He runs a damn company, but I can tell you, Sam," he leaned forward, his neck veins bulging, "DeWitt will make up for the loss Longstreth caused me, and you'll see why soon."
[483] "Write that down, Jonathan," Sam said. "This guy is digging his own grave... Collins, old friend, you invested 50,000 in international metal stocks. Where did you get all that money? With your salary, you couldn't afford it."
[484] "Mind your own business, Sam, or I'll break your neck..."
[485] Sam's large hand grabbed Collins' collar, bringing their faces inches apart. "I warn you, if your filthy mouth dares to utter another insult, I'll do exactly what you said and break your neck right here. Now get out of here, you bastard."
[486] Sam pushed him away, and Collins, enraged, couldn't say a word and stormed out the door. Sam shook himself off, cursed a few times, and called in the short-bearded Bolukus.
[487] The mind-reading artist had a thin, wolf-like Italian face and looked very tense. Sam stared at him with piercing eyes.
[488] "Listen to me," Sam's powerful finger pointed at Bolukus' collar, "I'll tell you straight, I don't have time to chat with you. Tell me, what do you know about Lestrade's murder?"
[489] Bolukus glanced at the broken mirror on the table and started shouting in Italian. He was terrified of Sam but refused to cooperate honestly. He spoke in a pretentious tone, "I know nothing. You won't get anything out of me or Cheryl."
[490] "Pure as a blank sheet of paper, is it? Innocent as a baby, is it?"
[491] "Listen, Detective, Lunsford was a scumbag who deserved this fate. He almost ruined Theresa's life. Everyone in Broadway knew him as a vampire, and it was only a matter of time before he got his comeuppance."
[492] "Familiar with Theresa?"
[493] "Who? Me? Of course, we've always been good friends."
[494] "Serving her every need, doing everything for her?"
[495] "What do you mean by that?"
[496] "Just that. Get out of here."
[497] Polux fumed but dared not say anything, and Joss mimicked Polux's walk as he stood up.
[498] Sam sneered and walked to the door, calling out, "DeWitt, come in for a minute. Just a minute."
[499] DeWitt calmed down and seemed as if nothing had happened. He noticed the broken mirror on the table as soon as he entered.
[500] "Whose mirror broke?" he asked absentmindedly.
[501] "Quite observant, isn't it? It's your wife's."
[502] DeWitt sat down and sighed. "Now this is bad. My wife will be complaining about this and that for weeks, and everyone will suffer. I think this is never-ending."
[503] "So superstitious, your wife?"
[504] "Extremely superstitious. You know, she has half-Spanish blood, and her mom is a typical Castilian Spaniard, while her dad is a Protestant. She was raised with a Castilian-style education, completely ignoring the Catholic teachings of the church. Fawn can be quite troublesome sometimes."
[505] Sam flicked a piece of glass off the table with his finger. "I suppose you don't believe in this stuff, right, DeWitt? I heard you're a shrewd and experienced businessman."
[506] DeWitt looked at Sam without hostility. "I know, my friend made some comments." He said mildly, "No, Sam, I certainly don't believe in that nonsense."
[507] Sam suddenly changed the subject: "DeWitt, I called you here to get your assurance that you will cooperate fully with my men and the county attorney's office investigators when they come to investigate."
[508] "You can count on it."
[509] "You know, we have to check all of Langestrit's business and personal correspondence, his bank accounts, and all the transaction records. When my people come here, you promise to help them as much as possible, right?"
[510] "Chief, I can assure you of that."
[511] "Good."
[512] Sam then ordered the sheep to be set free in the adjacent office and gave some instructions to Deputy Chief Pibody and a competent-looking assistant from the District Attorney's office before leaving the DeWitt-Lestrade Division.
[513] Sam's face was very dark.
[514] Act IX
[515] Hamlet Manor
[516] September 8th, Tuesday, 12:10 PM
[517] Rayn dropped some small wooden pieces into the fireplace, and the fire flared up immediately. In the flickering light, Bruno carefully observed the subtle changes in Rayn's expression. Rayn only smiled faintly, showing no obvious reaction. As for Sam, who had been talking non-stop about the story, he fell into a somewhat troubled silence.
[518] "Is that it, officer?"
[519] Sam made a gurgling sound in his throat.
[520] Rayne's eyelids drooped, and at that moment, there seemed to be an irresistible, enormous hypnotic force, and Rayne seemed to fall asleep just like that. The officer became flustered: "Did I not explain anything clearly...?" From his tone, Sam could feel that he believed that if there were any details he didn't explain thoroughly, it was because they were completely irrelevant to the ultimate outcome of the case. Sam was a bit of a cynic.
[521] Rene remained motionless. Bruno chuckled: "Sam, he can't hear you. He's got his eyes closed."
[522] Sam only then woke up. He moved his body forward a bit on the Elizabethan-era chair.
[523] Rene opened his eyes, looking at the two of them, and suddenly stood up, startling Bruno. He turned his body slightly towards Sam, with the firelight casting shadows on his chiseled profile. "I have a few questions for you, Chief. Did Dr. Slinger make any further discoveries during the autopsy?"
[524] "No," Sam said dejectedly. "The nicotine analysis confirmed Dr. Slinger's earlier suspicions, but we've made no progress in identifying the poison and its source."
[525] "Moreover," the prosecutor added, glancing at Rene, "the investigation into the needle and cork has yielded no clues, at least not yet."
[526] "Mr. Bruno, do you have a copy of Dr. Schilling's autopsy report?"
[527] The prosecutor produced a document and handed it to Rayn. Rayn bent over the fire, reading the report aloud quickly and selectively: "Cause of death: suffocation - blood not coagulated, dark red in color, hmm... central nervous system, especially the system controlling respiration, paralyzed, undoubtedly due to high concentration of nicotine poisoning... lungs and liver showed signs of congestion... brain showed signs of hemorrhage, hmm... the condition of the lungs indicates the victim had a considerable resistance to nicotine, indicating a long-term smoking habit. Based on the nicotine concentration in the body, a person with no nicotine resistance would be dead within a minute. The victim's resistance delayed the time of death... physical features: slight knee abrasion on the left, possibly from falling during the fit... appendectomy performed, scar indicates nine years ago; right index finger tip amputated, over twenty years ago... normal blood sugar, high brain alcohol content. Excellent physical condition in the early years, severe deterioration in later life... hmm, height of six feet one inch, weight of two hundred and eleven pounds... " Rayn finished reading and handed the report back to Bruno. "Thank you, prosecutor."
[528] He paced back to the fireplace, leaning against the rough oak mantel: "Didn't find anything in the garage reception room, did you?"
[529] "No."
[530] "I suppose the Lansdell residence in Seengelei was thoroughly searched, right?"
[531] "Oh, of course," Sam began to be a little distracted, winking at Bruno half-jokingly and half-seriously, "but we found nothing. Just a bunch of letters - all from his girlfriends, almost all written before March this year - and receipts and bills, all garbage. We couldn't get anything out of the servants either."
[532] "I assume his apartment in the city was also searched?"
[533] "Yes, we didn't miss that either. We even questioned his old sweethearts, but nothing came out of it."
[534] Rene looked at them both very calmly, his eyes steady and deep. "Inspector Sam, are you absolutely sure that the cork with the needle inserted was put into the victim's pocket while he was in the car? Not before?"
[535] Sam answered without hesitation: "We are one hundred percent certain, no other possibility. And I brought the weapon of interest, if you're interested."
[536] "Great, Inspector, you guessed it right," Rein's voice boomed with anticipation.
[537] Sam took a small glass bottle out of his coat pocket, tightly screwed on the lid. He handed the bottle to Rein. "Mr. Rein, you'd better not open it, I'm afraid there might be danger."
[538] Rein took the glass bottle to the fireplace and looked at it carefully for a long time. The needles on the cork, from the tip to the eye, were pitch-black and looked completely harmless. Rein sniffed again before returning the bottle to Sam. "It's clearly a homemade weapon, as Dr. Schiller said, a masterpiece... Was it raining heavily before the car arrived at the garage, with passengers getting off?"
[539] "Yes, it was pouring like a bucket of water."
[540] "Now, tell me - was there a passenger on the car who looked like a worker?"
[541] Sam's eyes widened, and Bruno's eyebrows furrowed in shock. "You mean... a worker?"
[542] "A janitor, construction worker, plasterer, or bricklayer—something like that."
[543] Sam was momentarily at a loss. "Well, no, there were all office workers on board, I don't know..."
[544] "Did you thoroughly check all the passengers?"
[545] "Yes," Sam replied, a bit irritated.
[546] "Trust me, Inspector, I'm not questioning your abilities... but just to be safe, I'll ask again: did you find anything unusual, either on the passengers, in the car, or in the room where the passengers left after they got off—everywhere relevant?"
[547] "I think I've made myself clear, Mr. Lane," Sam answered coldly.
[548] "But... nothing out of place, not in terms of location, weather conditions, this season, or people's identities?"
[549] "I don't understand what you're getting at."
[550] "For example, did you find any coats, evening gowns, or gloves?"
[551] "Oh, so that's it. There's only one person wearing a trench coat, but as we just mentioned, I personally checked, and there's nothing else you're talking about. I can assure you of that."
[552] At this moment, Rene's eyes glinted with excitement. He focused on Sam, then on Bruno, and then stretched out a lazy yawn. The firelight cast a massive shadow on the ancient walls, enveloping him. "Mr. Bruno, what's the view from the Public Prosecutor's Office?"
[553] Bruno coldly smiled: "It's clear, Mr. Rain, we don't have any specific leads. This case is very complex, involving many people and many possible motives. For example, Mrs. DeWitt is obviously involved with Lestrade, but Lestrade cheated on her with Cherry Brown and she hates Lestrade. From her past behavior - in short, it's quite unusual.
[554] "Mike Collins, a man with a reputation for being shrewd, unscrupulous, and easily provoked, has a clear motive for this as well."
[555] "Lord, this young man, like a revenge knight from an old storybook, might kill to protect his lover's honor." Here, Bruno sighed, "But Sam and I still think DeWitt is the most suspicious."
[556] Bruno sighed. "Nevertheless, Sam and I still believe that Mr. DeWitt is the most suspicious."
[557] "DeWitt," Rayne said clearly, his eyes fixed on Bruno's lips, "continue."
[558] "The problem is," Bruno frowned anxiously, "there's not a shred of direct evidence pointing to him - or anyone else, for that matter. No one has evidence of a crime."
[559] Sam added, "Anyone could have put the weapon in Lentz's pocket, not just Lentz's companions, but all the passengers on the car. That's why we're checking each one, and we find that none of them have any connection to Lentz, no clues at all."
[560] Bruno concluded, "That's why Sam and I are bold enough to come and visit you, Mr. Rayne. The last time we encountered the Kramer case, you made a brilliant analysis of the case, pointing out the truth that was always in front of us but never noticed by us, helping us solve the case. This time, we hope you will again lend a hand and guide us."
[561] Bruno responded with a shrug. Rayne's voice boomed, and both men turned to him.
[562] "Gentlemen," Rayne said, looking at them with interest, "the whole thing is quite clear, I think you both know that."
[563] The impact of this calm statement was like a lightning strike, causing Bruno's jaw to drop and Sam to stagger, trying to regain his composure.
[564] Sam jumped up. "Clear!" he exclaimed. "Oh, Mr. Rayne, you mean -"
[565] "Just calm down, Sam, sherrif," Rayne said softly. "You're like Hamlet's father's ghost, shocked like 'a trembling condemned man.' Yes, gentlemen, the whole thing is quite clear. If everything Sam sherrif said is true, then I believe the case points in one direction."
[566] "I must be blind," Sam gasped, looking at Rayne with distrust.
[567] "You mean," Bruno asked, as if drained, "you know who killed Langstroth based on what Sam Inspector just said?"
[568] Rayne's nose twitched. "I mean – I believe I know... Bruno, without evidence."
[569] "Oh, I see!" The two men exclaimed in unison, and exchanged a meaningful glance.
[570] "Gentlemen, I understand your skepticism, but for me, this is not baseless speculation," Rayne said with a voice that had a kind of hypnotic magic and a strange persuasive quality. "At this stage, I have reason enough not to reveal the identity of the enigmatic figure you've been searching for – let's call him X for now – and I feel there may be a co-conspirator involved in this murder case."
[571] "But, Mr. Renn," Bruno said anxiously, "time is—"
[572] Renn stood calmly, looking like an Indian in the blazing firelight, with a smile fading from his lips and a stern expression like a solid marble statue. His lips barely moved, but his voice was clear: "Delay? There is danger, but the danger is doubled if the truth is revealed prematurely."
[573] Sam stood glumly, clearly dissatisfied, while Bruno remained stunned.
[574] "For now, please don't force me to reveal it. Can you help me with something?..." Renn's voice took on a touch of impatience as Sam and Bruno's faces remained skeptical, "Can you give me a clearer photo of the victim, preferably from before the incident? You can mail it or have someone deliver it."
[575] "Sure, no problem," Bruno said softly, shifting his weight from one foot to the other like a scolded schoolboy.
[576] "Please keep me updated on the case's progress," Rine continued calmly, "unless... you're not willing to discuss this case with me any further." He fixed his gaze on the two of them for a moment, and the original joy in his eyes returned.
[577] The two men hastily denied, looking less than sincere.
[578] "Quince will take down any information for you if you call, even if I'm not home," Rine said, pulling a bell on the soot-covered mantelpiece, and the red-faced, uniformed, and pot-bellied old man appeared like a goblin, "Would you like to join me for lunch? Please excuse me if I'm not able to entertain you both, but if either of you or anyone else visits, please let me know. Goodbye, Mr. Bruno. Goodbye, Inspector Sam."
[579] Bruno and Sam followed the butler in silence, stopping at the door and turning back to Rine, who stood by his ancient fireplace, smiling gently at them and bidding them farewell as if from a distant and unreal world.
[580] Act II
[581] Scene I
[582] District Attorney's Office
[583] September 9, Tuesday, 9:20 a.m.
[584] The next morning, Bruno and Sam sat across from each other at Bruno's desk, two stubborn men arguing over the mysterious murder case, arguing fiercely. Bruno's cluttered desk, once neat and orderly, was now a mess of files and documents. Sam's naturally flat nose, flattened even more by the morning breeze and the lack of progress in the case, was even flatter.
[585] "Honestly," Sam growled, "I've hit a dead end. I've checked for poison, corks, and needles, but found nothing. Nicotine doesn't seem to have been purchased, probably made privately or distilled from insecticide, which leaves us with no leads. As for your dear Mr. Rene - I believe it's a waste of time."
[586] Bruno countered, "Don't be so hasty, Sam. I don't think it's a waste of time." He spread his hands, "I think you've misjudged this man. Yes, he's an odd character, living in such an antique-filled place, talking about Shakespeare... "
[587] "Well, I'm just telling it like it is," Sam said gloomily. "I think he's a fraud, just playing hide-and-seek with us. He claims to know who killed Langstroth, but it's just a gimmick to entertain the audience."
[588] "Sam, that's not fair to Mr. Reine," Bruno defended, "After all, he knows he can't disclose his findings without evidence and hopes to pursue further. He must also know that he has to prove his deductions eventually. No, I'm inclined to believe that he knows what he's talking about—he really discovered something—but for some necessary reasons, he can't reveal it now."
[589] Sam slammed his hand on the table. "What do you mean by that? Am I an idiot? Are you an idiot?—What did he discover? Great discovery? Tell you what, he knows nothing! I'll bet he doesn't know anything, for God's sake, you thought the same yesterday... "
[590] "Can't I change my mind? Can't you?" Bruno interrupted, then felt a bit embarrassed. "We shouldn't forget, he was spot-on in the Kramer case when it was at a standstill. Now with this damn murder case, I won't give up any chance to crack it, no matter how slim. Besides, I've asked him to help with the investigation, so I can't just ask him to leave without a word. No, no, Sam, we have to proceed, and it won't have any bad consequences... Anything new?"
[591] Sam tore a cigarette in half. "Collins is still making a fuss. My men just reported that Collins has found DeWitt three times since Saturday, he wants DeWitt to pay him, of course. Anyway, I'll keep an eye on him, but it's DeWitt's business…"
[592] Bruno lazily sorted through a pile of letters, tossing two into the filing folder. The third, in a cheap envelope, made him jump up from his chair. Bruno read the letter while Sam squinted at him.
[593] "Oh, God, Sam," Bruno exclaimed, "this is what we've been looking for - oh, what now? He interrupted the secretary who had barged in.
[594] The secretary handed over a business card, which Bruno snatched up. "He's here, what for?" He lowered and slowed his voice, "Well, Barny, bring him in…Sam, sit still, don't go anywhere. There's something in this letter, but first let's see what this Swiss guy wants to do. It's Inveriari who came to see us."
[595] The secretary opened the door, and indeed, the tall Swiss merchant entered, smiling. Inveriari's outfit was as flashy as ever, dressed in a standard morning suit, a flower pinned to the lapel, and his cane tucked under his arm.
[596] "Good morning, Mr. Impieri," Bruno said calmly, though the letter had been put away. He rested his hands on the edge of the table. Sam simply greeted him.
[597] "Good morning, respected prosecutor. Good morning, Mr. Sam. I won't trouble you for long, Mr. Bruno," Impieri said, sitting in the leather chair beside Bruno's desk. "My business in America is over, and I'm heading back to Switzerland."
[598] "Oh, is that so?" Bruno glanced at Sam, who stared at Impieri's broad back.
[599] "I've already booked a ticket for tonight's ship," Impieri said, slightly frowning. "I've also called the moving company to pack my luggage, but your men suddenly came out of the house where I was staying and wouldn't let me leave!"
[600] "Evicting Mr. DeWitt's house, is it, Mr. Impieri?"
[601] Mr. Inperialey shook his head, looking very agitated. "No, I'm leaving America, but your men said they couldn't let me take my luggage, and that's a problem for me, Mr. Bruno. I'm a businessman, and there are urgent matters at my company in Bern that require my immediate attention. Why should I be delayed like this? Of course -"
[602] Bruno tapped on the desk. "Now listen to me, Mr. Inperialey. I don't know how things are done in your country, but it seems you haven't realized yet that you're involved in an American murder case. Listen, it's an American murder case."
[603] "I know, but -"
[604] "No buts, Mr. Inperialey. I'm sorry, but you have to stay in this country until the Lengstruth murder case is solved, or at least until you have an official permit. Of course, you can move out of Mr. DeWitt's house and stay wherever you want - I can't stop you, but you have to be available for questioning."
[605] Mr. Inperialey stood up stiffly, his cheerful expression gone, his face contorted. "I've said it would affect my business."
[606] Bruno shrugged.
[607] "Very well," Fioriello put on his hat, his face as red as the flames of the Rine's hearth. "I'm going to see my consul, Mr. Bruno, to demand justice. You don't know it, but I'm a Swiss citizen, and you have no right to keep me here. Goodbye!"
[608] He nodded slightly and walked out. Bruno smiled and said, "Anyway, I would advise you to cancel your ticket, Mr. Fioriello, it's a waste of money..."
[609] "Come on, come on," Bruno perked up. "Don't mind him, let's sit down, Sam, and take a look at this letter." He took out a letter from his pocket and opened it in front of Sam. Sam first looked at the end of the letter - no signature. The letter was written on cheap lined paper, with black ink, and there was no deliberate attempt to conceal the handwriting. The letter was addressed directly to the prosecutor.
[610] I was on the train when Lansdorff was killed. As for who the killer is, I know a thing or two. Prosecutor sir, I'm willing to tell you everything I know, but I'm afraid the killer suspects that I know something, and I feel like someone is watching me.
[611] If you're willing to meet me on Wednesday evening at 11 pm, or send someone to meet me, I'll tell you everything I know. The location is the waiting room at Weehawken Pier. You'll know who I am then, and I'll identify myself. Prosecutor, for my safety, please don't leak the news, and don't tell anyone about this letter. I'm afraid the killer will know what I told you, and I might lose my life because I performed my duty as an American citizen.
[612] Will you guarantee my safety? When we meet on Wednesday evening, you will be very satisfied. This is very important, and I don't want to be seen running around during the day to report to the police.
[613] Sam carefully picked up the letter and put it back on the table, and carefully checked the envelope. "Last night's postmark from New York Weehawken area," Sam whispered, "dirty hands, a lot of fingerprints on it. One of the passengers on the train back to New Jersey ... Bruno, I can't tell if this is real or fake, it could be a prank or a serious matter, I don't know what to do, what do you think?"
[614] "It's hard to say," Bruno looked at the ceiling, "it looks like a lead worth pursuing. Anyway, I'll be there on time, it doesn't matter," he got up and paced around the room, "Sam, I have a feeling that this trip might be quite rewarding. The guy who wrote the letter, whoever he is, didn't sign it, so it looks very real. Look at what he wrote in the letter, he said one thing and then another, and he was a little self-important because he suddenly became so important. Moreover, he was trembling with fear when he talked about the danger of being exposed. In short, this letter has all the basic elements of a typical informant letter - tedious, nagging, and nervous - you see, he even misspelled the word "meet" and forgot to add a stroke to the letter "t" in many places. Anyway, the more I think about it, the more I feel like we've hit the jackpot."
[615] "Well ..." Sam hesitated but soon became excited, "This letter is a heavy blow to Mr. Reins. At least, we won't have to listen to his so-called analysis and advice anymore."
[616] "Leave that to me, Sam. We have to act quickly," Bruno said, satisfied as he rubbed his hands together. "Here's what we'll do: you contact the prosecutor of Hudson County on the other side of the Hudson River and ask him to have the New Jersey police monitor the Whacken terminus to avoid any trouble caused by jurisdictional issues. Everyone will be in plain clothes, Sam - will you go too?"
[617] "Whoever wants to stop me can try it," Sam grinned roughly.
[618] As soon as Sam left, Bruno picked up the phone on the table and dialed Hamlet Manor. He waited on the line, calm, no, actually feeling an incredibly peaceful sense of tranquility. The bell rang on the other end of the line.
[619] "Hello, Hamlet Manor? Is this Mr. Rain... I'm Bruno prosecutor... Hello, who is it?"
[620] A shrill, quivering voice answered: "I'm Quasi, Bruno, Mr. Rain is right here."
[621] "Ah, that's right – I forgot. Tell Mr. Lane that there's more than just him who knows who killed Longstreth," Bruno's tone was filled with a sense of victory.
[622] He listened as Quixy relayed his words to Mr. Lane.
[623] "He said 'That's great!'" Quixy's voice echoed again, "So, what's next?"
[624] "Tell him there's more than just him who knows who killed Longstreth," Bruno's tone was filled with a sense of victory.
[625] He listened as Quixy relayed Mr. Lane's response, "You tell Bruno that this is great news – word for word. Is the killer turning themselves in?"
[626] Bruno told Quasi about the anonymous letter and its contents. There was a moment of silence on the other end of the phone, and then Reine's calm voice spoke again.
[627] "Tell Mr. Bruno that I'm sorry I can't speak with him directly. Ask him if I can attend tonight's meeting?"
[628] "Oh, of course." Bruno said to Quasi, "Um - Quasi, did Mr. Reine seem surprised?"
[629] Bruno heard a strange laugh - a sly chuckle from a well-fed mind. Then, Quasi spoke in a jokingly trembling voice, "No, he was happy about the change of circumstances. He always says he looks forward to the unexpected, he -"
[630] But Bruno simply said goodbye and hung up the phone.
[631] Second Act
[632] Whiskey Dock
[633] September 9th, Tuesday, 11:40 PM
[634] On a normally clear evening, the lights of New York City would illuminate the night sky, but on this Tuesday night, the entire city was shrouded in a thick blanket of fog that had persisted throughout the day and into the night. From the New Jersey ferry terminal, only the occasional flicker of distant lights and a gray wall of fog could be seen on the river. Sometimes, a ferry would suddenly emerge from the fog, its dim lights barely visible on the deck; ghostly little boats would rise and fall, drifting in the mist; the foghorns would sound, carefully maintaining the channel, but their voices seemed swallowed by the fog almost immediately.
[635] Behind the Whiskey Dock ferry terminal, a large warehouse-like building housed ten or so people. Most of them stood silently, observing the situation around them. In the center, standing like Napoleon, was Bruno the prosecutor. He nervously checked his watch every ten seconds and paced around the hollow floor. Sam was looking around, keeping an eye on the various doors and the occasional person who walked into the waiting room. The large waiting room seemed empty.
[636] Near this group of law enforcement officers, Mr. Jules Renard sat quietly. His elegant and refined appearance drew curious and even amused glances from passengers waiting and passing by. He paid no attention to the surroundings, with his long, slender fingers intertwined on the handle of his walking stick, which was placed between his knees. He wore a black overcoat with a double cape, which hung loosely; his thick black hair was topped with a black felt hat. Sam couldn't help but glance at Renard every now and then, for he had never seen a man like Renard - from his clothing and hairstyle, so old-fashioned, but from his face and physique, so youthful. Renard's erect posture and full, powerful physique seemed to be around thirty-five years old, and his calm demeanor made people want to look at him more. Of course, Renard himself did not intend to attract these curious glances - in fact, he did not notice any passerby.
[637] His sharp eyes were fixed on Bruno's lips.
[638] Bruno approached and sat down next to Renard, a bit annoyed. "We've been waiting for over forty-five minutes," he complained. "It seems we've wasted our time asking you to come here. Of course, for us, we have to stay here until dawn anyway, but honestly, I'm starting to think we're being foolish."
[639] "Bruno, you should be getting more worried," Renard's voice was clear and melodious. "You have good reason to be worried."
[640] "You mean -" Bruno frowned, ready to continue, but suddenly closed his mouth. Sam stopped pacing. A piercing cry came from outside the pier.
[641] "Mr. Bruno, is something wrong?" Vance asked mildly.
[642] Bruno was still listening, leaning forward. "You can't hear it, of course... Mr. Vance, someone is shouting that someone has fallen into the water!"
[643] Vance stood up like a cat. Sam shouted, "There's an incident at the quay," and then turned around to yell, "I'll go check it out."
[644] Bruno also stood up, a little hesitant. "Sam, leave a few people to guard here. It could be a diversion, and the person we're waiting for may come at this moment."
[645] Sam rushed to the door, followed closely by Vance, with six detectives running after them.
[646] They rushed onto the wooden floor outside and stopped to determine the correct direction of the noise. At the far end of the covered dock, a ferry had arrived, scraping the wooden posts at the dockside as it tried to align itself with the iron staircase on the shore. Several passengers jumped nervously off the ship as Sam, Ren, and the detectives arrived. The word "Mohawk" was written in gold letters on the upper deck of the ferry, and a crowd of passengers were gathered on the lower deck, leaning over the railing to look down at the dark, misty water below. Passengers in the cabin peeked out of the windows, looking down at the black water shrouded in fog.
[647] Three ferry workers pushed their way through the crowd to the railing. Ren glanced at his gold watch and saw that it was 11:40.
[648] Sam jumped onto the deck and grabbed a skinny old sailor by the arm.
[649] "I'm a police officer!" Sam's voice was loud. "What's going on?"
[650] The old sailor looked quite alarmed. "Someone has fallen into the water, officer. It seems like it happened just as the Mohawk was about to dock, from the upper deck."
[651] "Who is the person who fell - does anyone know?"
[652] "No one knows."
[653] "Come up here, Reen," Sam called to Reen, who was still on shore. "The staff will retrieve the person, and we'll check the location where they fell."
[654] They pushed their way through the crowd, heading towards the cabin door. Suddenly, Sam called out and waved his arms, as a small man was trying to disembark from the upper deck of the ferry.
[655] "Hey, DeWitt, come over here!"
[656] The small man wrapped in a long coat looked up at the sound of Sam's voice, hesitated for a moment upon seeing Sam, and then walked over obediently. His face was a little pale, and he sighed softly. "Inspector Sam," he said slowly, "how did you get here?"
[657] "A little business," Sam replied vaguely, but his gaze was sharp. "And you? How did you end up here?"
[658] DeWitt inserted his hand into the left pocket of his coat and shuddered. "I was on my way home," he said. "I don't know what's going on."
[659] "We're investigating," Sam said amiably. "We'll find out soon. Let's go together. By the way, this is Mr. Philo Vance, who is assisting us with the case. Mr. Vance is an actor and a well-known celebrity. Mr. Vance, this is Mr. DeWitt, a partner of Longstreet."
[660] Mr. Vance nodded politely in greeting. DeWitt's suspicious gaze fell on the actor's face, and he immediately showed a look of sudden realization mixed with unusual excitement. "Oh, Mr. Vance, it's an honor to meet you in person."
[661] Sam, standing beside him, seemed unaffected by the atmosphere and looked grim. The detectives behind him patiently waited for instructions. Sam looked around, as if searching for someone, and muttered under his breath before shrugging his shoulders.
[662] "Let's go," Sam said abruptly, and his bulky figure led the way into the crowd.
[663] The cabin was in chaos. Sam climbed up the brass-handled staircase to the cabin, followed by the others, and passed through the oval upper deck through a door on the north side, reaching the dim upper deck. The detectives turned on their flashlights and began to examine the deck. In the middle of the deck and the bow, just behind the wheelhouse, a few feet away from the bow, Sam found a long scratch that was easy to overlook. The detectives gathered around and focused their flashlights on it. The scratch extended from the intersection of the iron railings at the bow to the back of the deck, through the deck, and all the way to a small room in the northwest corner of the cabin, or more accurately, a recessed compartment in the cabin. The west and south walls of the room shared with the cabin, the north wall was only a thin board, and the east wall was completely open. The flashlight followed the scratch and found that the end of the scratch indeed came from the small room inside. There was a locked toolbox hanging on the wall, some life-saving equipment, a broom, a bucket, and some miscellaneous items. The open side was blocked by an iron chain, preventing anyone from entering.
[664] "Go find the key. Check inside and see if you can find anything," two detectives were ordered.
[665] "You, Jim, go down and ask everyone to stay on board."
[666] Sam, on the other hand, walked with Rayne to the railing at the bow, with DeWitt following. The deck extended two and a half feet beyond the railing. Sam examined the deck scratch with a flashlight and said to Rayne, "Mr. Rayne, that's a bit unusual, isn't it? This is a trace left by the back of the heel. In my opinion, this is a heavy body being dragged across the deck, causing the shoe heel to rub against the deck. That means, it may be another murder case."
[667] Rayne stared at Sam's face in the dim flashlight for a while before solemnly nodding.
[668] The three of them stood up and leaned over the railing to look down. Below, there was a commotion. Sam glanced at DeWitt's expression, who was now composed and seemed to have given up.
[669] A police boat had stopped in front of the ferry, and several policemen quickly climbed onto the slippery wooden piles. Two powerful searchlights were suddenly turned on, illuminating the entire ferry and the entire dock, which emerged clearly from the fog, and even the upper deck where they were sharing quite a bit of light. The searchlights slowly swept along the lower deck, leaving no dead angle. Since the lower deck extended forward and tightly abutted the slippery wooden piles of the dock, the searchlights could not reach the bottom of the water. The dock staff and workers stood or squatted on the wooden piles, shouting at the ferry's steering room above. Suddenly, the sound of engines roared, and the ferry began to slide, moving slowly from the north side of the dock to the south side. The captain and pilot in the steering room were doing their best to move the ferry away from the area where someone fell into the water.
[670] "He's probably squashed like a pancake," Sam said matter-of-factly. "He fell down right when the ship hit the pile, and he was stuck between the ship and the pile, and the ship kept pushing forward, so he was probably buried under the ship. This is really something to see...Wow, it worked. I can see the water."
[671] As the loud ferry slid away, the dark and foul-smelling oily water emerged, floating with garbage and bubbles. Soon, a long rope with an iron hook suddenly appeared from the top of the wooden pole, and the police and wharf staff's salvage operation officially began.
[672] DeWitt stood between Sam and Rayne, his attention fully drawn to the salvage operation below. At this time, a detective approached Sam.
[673] "What's going on?" Sam asked roughly.
[674] "Sir, the toolbox is empty, and we couldn't find anything suspicious in the room."
[675] "I know. Tell everyone to be careful not to damage the scuff mark on the deck."
[676] Sam issued commands calmly while keeping a keen eye on DeWitt's every move. The slim securities merchant was very focused, his left hand gripping the exposed iron railing tightly, his right elbow leaning against the railing, and his whole upper right arm in an unnatural position.
[677] "What's wrong, Mr. DeWitt? Your hand is injured?"
[678] DeWitt slowly turned his head, looked at his right hand, smiled faintly, and then extended his right hand to Sam. Rayne also leaned over. DeWitt's index finger had a wound that extended down an inch and a half from the first joint, forming a hard, dry blood clot.
[679] "I accidentally cut myself on the gym equipment at the club earlier this evening."
[680] "Oh!"
[681] "Doctor Morris at the club took care of the wound and told me to be careful. It still hurts a little here."
[682] Suddenly, a series of cheers erupted below. Sam and DeWitt hurriedly leaned back on the railing, and Rein, who couldn't hear the sound, followed suit and looked down.
[683] "Found it! Take it easy! Take it easy!"
[684] One of the ropes that coiled into the water from the top of the stake seemed to have caught onto something below the surface.
[685] Three minutes later, a wet, limp thing emerged from the river, and there was another shriek from the lower deck - a reflexive shriek.
[686] "Let's go down!" Sam blurted out, and the three of them turned and ran for the hatch. DeWitt led the way, but as he reached for the door handle, he let out a cry of pain.
[687] "What's wrong?" Sam asked urgently. DeWitt grimaced at his right hand, and Sam and Rayne saw that DeWitt's fingertips were bleeding in several places.
[688] "I accidentally used my right hand to open the door," DeWitt groaned. "The wound split open, and Dr. Morris warned me it would."
[689] "Don't worry, you'll be fine," Sam said gruffly, and he darted past DeWitt, leading the way down the stairs. He glanced back, and DeWitt was carefully wrapping his right hand in a handkerchief from his chest pocket. Rayne's chin was buried in the collar of his cloak, and his eyes were hidden in shadow. Rayne comforted DeWitt, and the two of them followed Sam down the stairs.
[690] The three of them crossed the starboard lower deck and emerged onto the deck in front of the cabin, where rescue personnel had laid out a tarp. The soft, squishy thing they had retrieved from the river lay on the tarp, floating in a small, foul-smelling puddle of water. It was the body of a man, barely recognizable due to the blood and damage to the corpse. His head and face were a mass of rot; from the unnatural contortions, it was likely that his spine was broken; his arms were shockingly flattened, as if run over by a roller.
[691] Lane's face, which had been pale to begin with, was now completely devoid of color, but he still made an effort to remain calm and focused on the gruesome scene. Sam, who had seen many such scenes before, still felt uncomfortable and muttered under his breath. Dewitt, on the other hand, glanced at it once and quickly turned away, his whole face turning green. Besides the three of them, the dock workers, the ferry captain and the pilot, the detectives, and the police officers were all present. No one spoke, and they all stood there blankly, staring at the corpse.
[692] There was a loud shout from the other side of the ferry, and the passengers were ushered into the long cabin by the police.
[693] The body was lying face down, with its lower half not bent back and to the side like a normal human body, and its broken head resting on the deck. A black hat with a brim was lying on the canvas, dripping water.
[694] Sam knelt down and, with one hand, pushed the body. It was soft and floppy, like a bag of meat. Sam half-turned it over, and a detective stepped forward to help. As the face turned upwards, it was clear that it was a red-haired, large man with a distorted face that was impossible to recognize. Sam let out a surprised gasp. The man was wearing a dark blue coat, with black leather pockets on the edges, and two rows of brass buttons running down the front. Sam grabbed the black hat from the canvas - it was indeed a ticket collector's hat, with a gold number 2101 on the brim and the words "Third Avenue Subway" in gold.
[695] "It could be..." Sam exclaimed, then stopped abruptly. He looked up at Lane, who was bending over, staring intently at the hat in Sam's hand.
[696] Sam put down the hat and, without hesitation, reached into the inner pocket of the deceased's coat. He pulled out a wet, cheap leather wallet. He opened it and immediately jumped up, his ugly face lighting up.
[697] "That's it!" Sam shouted, quickly scanning the surroundings.
[698] Bruno's short and stout figure was running towards the pier from the subway station, his coat flapping in the wind. Several plainclothes police officers followed behind him.
[699] Sam quickly turned to a detective and ordered, "Immediately double the police presence and closely monitor all passengers on the ferry!" He stamped his foot and waved the wet wallet in his hand, "Bruno! Hurry up! We've found the person we've been waiting for!"
[700] Bruno ran even faster. He boarded the ship, glanced at the corpse and the onlookers, including Ren and Dewitt, and asked breathlessly, "What about - the person who wrote the letter?"
[701] "Exactly," Sam said hoarsely, tapping the ground with his toe. "Someone beat us to it."
[702] Bruno's eyes widened and he looked at the corpse again, at the copper buttons on the coat, and at the hat lying on the deck. "The ticket seller..." He took off his own hat; despite the freezing cold, Bruno wiped the sweat off his forehead with a silk handkerchief. "Sam, are you sure?"
[703] Sam took out a soggy card from the wallet and handed it to Bruno, who answered.
[704] It was a circular identification card issued by the Third Avenue Electric Company, with a stamp bearing the number 2101 and the signature of the holder.
[705] The signature was quite messy, but it could be clearly recognized as "Charles Wood."
[706] Act III
[707] Whipchen Station
[708] September 9, Tuesday, 11:58 PM
[709] The Whipchen Station waiting room, the terminus of the West Coast Line, was an ancient, drafty two-story building that looked like a giant barn from Gulliver's Travels. The exposed steel beams formed a strange aesthetic pattern overhead. Climbing the stairs to the second floor, a platform extended along the wall, leading to the tracks. A passageway along the platform led to several small offices. Everywhere was a dirty shade of gray.
[710] The body of the conductor Charles Wood was carried on a stretcher covered in canvas, still dripping with water. Through the echoing, empty waiting room, it was taken up to the second floor, along the platform, and into the stationmaster's office. The New Jersey police had cordoned off the entire waiting room, preventing anyone from entering or leaving. Under the watchful eyes of the police, all the passengers from the south side of the Whipchen ferry were led through a corridor formed by two rows of policemen to the waiting room at the terminus. Under the strict supervision of the police, they quietly awaited the actions of Sam and Bruno.
[711] Sam orders the Maeve ferry to be locked at the dock and not to sail. The ferry company immediately changes the sailing schedule after an emergency meeting. Despite the thick fog, ships continue to come and go at the dock; the railway company is also allowed to operate normally, but the temporary ticket office has been set up in the garage, and passengers have to take a longer route to board the ferry from the waiting room. As for the Maeve ferry, which is prohibited from sailing, it is brightly lit on board, with a row of policemen and police officers standing blackly. Except for the police and relevant personnel, no one else is allowed to board. In the stationmaster's office on the second floor, a small group of people are gathered around the corpse. Bruno is busy making phone calls, the first call being to Hudson County Prosecutor Reilly's home. In the phone call, he briefly explains to Reilly that the deceased was a witness to the Lunsford murder case - a case that occurred in Bruno's jurisdiction - and therefore, although the location of Wood's murder belongs to the jurisdiction of New Jersey, he hopes that Reilly will allow him to conduct the initial investigation. Reilly agrees, and Bruno immediately dials the New York Police Department, where Sam Chief of Police takes over the phone and orders some detectives to be immediately dispatched.
[712] Reen quietly sits in the chair, carefully watching Bruno's lips as he speaks and the pale-faced DeWitt - forgotten in the corner - and Sam shouting into the phone.
[713] It is not until Sam hangs up the phone that Reen speaks: "Mr. Bruno."
[714] Bruno, who is walking towards the corpse, looks at the terrible body with a gloomy expression, and turns his head to look at Reen when he hears his name, with a glimmer of hope in his eyes.
[715] "Mr. Bruno," Reen says, "have you carefully checked Wood's signature - his signature on the identification certificate?"
[716] "You mean…"
[717] "I think," Reen said mildly, "that our first task now is to prove that Wood was the author of the anonymous letter. Sam seems to think that Wood's signature and the letter's handwriting are from the same person, and I'm not doubting Sam's judgment, but I think it would be best to have an expert do the identification."
[718] Sam frowned uncomfortably: "The handwriting is exactly the same, Mr. Reen. Don't overthink it." He knelt beside the corpse, treating it like a mannequin in a clothing store. Finally, he found two crumpled and wet papers in the dead man's pocket: one was an accident report for a third-avenue trolley accident that occurred this afternoon, which Wood had signed; the other was a sealed letter with a stamp on it, which Sam tore open and handed to Bruno. Bruno carefully read the letter and then passed it to Reen. It was a letter applying for correspondence courses in traffic engineering. Reen carefully examined the handwriting and signature on both papers.
[719] "Mr. Bruno, do you have the anonymous letter on you?"
[720] Bruno rummaged through his wallet and found the letter. Reen spread the three papers on the table beside him and compared them closely. After a while, he chuckled and returned the papers to Bruno.
[721] "I'm sorry, Inspector," he said, "there's no doubt that these handwriting and signatures are from the same person. Now we know that the accident report, the application to the correspondence school, and the anonymous letter were all written by Wood... but since it's so important to confirm this, even though Inspector Sam's opinion is so unwavering, I think we should have an expert's opinion as well!"
[722] Sam grumbles unhappily, kneeling back in front of the body. Bruno puts the three papers back in his wallet and dials the phone again: "Dr. Shilling?... Hello, is this the doctor? I'm Bruno, at the Whipken Terminal Station, in the stationmaster's office. Yes, yes, behind the ferry terminal... right now... Okay, then you'll come as soon as you finish what you're doing... at 4 o'clock? That's fine, I'll take the body to the Hudson County morgue, and you can go there directly... Yes, I insist on you personally checking it. The deceased's name is Charles Wood, the ticket seller on the Long Island train."
[723] "I may be meddling too much," Raine said, sitting in the chair, "Mr. Bruno, is it possible that someone on the crew of the Mohawk or the staff of the trolley may have seen or spoken to Wood before he boarded the ship?"
[724] "Good point, Mr. Raine, they may not have left yet." Bruno picks up the phone again and dials the New York ferry terminal.
[725] "I'm Bruno, the prosecutor from the New York District Attorney's Office, I'm at the Whipken Terminal Station, where a murder has just occurred - oh, you've heard about it - we need your help here... good, the deceased is the ticket seller for the third-avenue trolley on 42nd Street, Wood, with service number 2101. Anyone who saw him or spoke to him tonight, please come here... about an hour ago, yes... and, when they come, can you send a patrol officer with them? There will be a police boat coming to pick them up."
[726] As soon as Bruno hung up the phone, he dispatched a detective to notify the harbor police on the Mohawk to take action immediately.
[727] "Now, Mr. Reen," Bruno rubbed his hands together, "while Sergeant Sam is examining the body, would you like to come down with me? There's still a lot of work to do."
[728] Reen got up, looking at DeWitt, who was standing alone in the corner. "Perhaps," Reen's clear baritone said, "Mr. DeWitt might also like to join us? This place won't be pleasant for him."
[729] Bruno's eyes sparkled behind his glasses, a smile playing on his otherwise serious face. "Yes, yes, of course. Mr. DeWitt, if you're willing, come along too!” The small stockbroker looked gratefully at Reen, dressed in a cloak, and quietly followed the two men as they walked down the stairs.
[730] The three marched down the stairs in a row, like a parade. Bruno raised his hand to get everyone's attention: "The captain and the pilot of the Mohawk, please come over."
[731] Two people stepped forward with heavy steps.
[732] "I am the navigator - Sam Adams," the navigator was strong and muscular, with a head of thick black hair, like a bull.
[733] "Wait, where is Jonas? Jonas!" - The detective in charge of taking statements ran over, holding a small notebook - "You're responsible for recording... Okay, Adams, let's first confirm the identity of the deceased. Did you see the body when it was placed on the deck?"
[734] "Of course I did."
[735] "Have you ever seen this person before?"
[736] "I've seen him at least a hundred times," the navigator tugged at his pants, "We were quite familiar. Although his face was mangled, I swear by the Bible that he is Wood, the ticket seller for the trolley."
[737] "Why are you so sure?"
[738] The navigator lifted his hat and scratched his head. "Why – there's no why, I just know. The same height, same red hair, same clothes – I can't say why, but I know, and moreover, we even talked tonight on the ship."
[739] "Oh! You talked, where? – In the steering room? I don't think passengers are allowed to chat in the steering room, Adams, tell me from the beginning."
[740] Adams cleared his throat, spat into the spittoon, and glanced nervously at the thin, copper-skinned man standing next to him – the captain of the ferry, before speaking: "Well, I've known Charles Wood for years, almost nine years, right, captain?" – The captain nodded confidently, also spat into the spittoon, and hit the spittoon perfectly – "I guess he lives in the Whipken area, as he always takes the 10:45 ferry home after work."
[741] "Wait a minute," Bruno nods at Reen, "did he take the 10:45 ferry tonight too?"
[742] Adams says unhappily, "I was just getting to that. He still took the 10:45 ferry tonight, and just like his usual habit, he climbed up to the top deck of the passenger area, talking about how beautiful the night was."
[743] "This is interesting," Bruno says, "very interesting, but you have to be more concise, Adams—you know, it's not a serialized novel in the newspaper."
[744] "Oh, am I going too slow?" the pilot tugs at his pants again, "I said—right, Wood took the 10:45 ferry tonight, climbed up to the top deck of the passenger area, right by the starboard side, just like he always does. He called out, 'Ahoy! Sam!' because I'm a crew member, he always calls me that, you know, to make a joke and pass the time."
[745] The ferry captain suddenly elbows Adams in the beer belly, causing Adams to cry out in surprise. "You're telling a fairy tale, no one can understand it," the captain speaks in a low voice, the echo in the room rumbling, "Get to the point, so it won't take a hundred years to tell."
[746] Adams stomped his feet in anger at his superior, "You're hitting my belly again - "
[747] "Alright, alright!" Bruno shouted to stop, "Stop arguing. Are you the captain of the Mochica?"
[748] "Yes," the thin captain was very self-assured, "Captain Sart, sailing on this river for twenty-one years."
[749] "Did you stay in the wheelhouse the whole time? When Adamson yelled, did you see Wood himself?"
[750] "I couldn't help but see him."
[751] "Are you sure it was 10:45?"
[752] "Yes."
[753] "Did you see Wood again after that?"
[754] "No, until he was fished out of the river like a fish."
[755] "Are you sure it was Wood who died?"
[756] "I'm not done yet," Adams interjected angrily. "Wood said something else. He said he couldn't take another trip today—he had an appointment in New Jersey."
[757] "Are you sure, Captain Sart? Did you hear that?"
[758] "That's the first sensible thing Adams has said all night, yes, sir. It was Wood—I've seen him a hundred times."
[759] "Adams, you said he couldn't take another trip tonight, so you mean he usually stays on the boat all day, doesn't get off until he's back on land?"
[760] "Not always, but sometimes the guy's in a good mood, especially on summer evenings, he'll take an extra trip."
[761] "All right, gentlemen."
[762] Just as the two men turned away, they were called back. It was Rayne, who rubbed his chin with a look of amusement.
[763] "Excuse me, Bruno, sir," Rayne said with a smile, "may I ask them a question?"
[764] "Of course, Rayne, sir, go ahead, don't be shy."
[765] "Thank you. Adams, Captain Sart," - the two crewmen looked at Rayne, their jaws dropping at the sight of the shawl, black hat, and the grotesque cane - "after you finished talking, did either of you see Wood leave his usual spot?"
[766] "Yes, I did," Adams answered promptly. "We received the signal to take the ship out, and Wood waved at us before returning to the top deck with the awning."
[767] "That's right," Captain Sart boomed in agreement.
[768] "Can you see that area from the steering room when the lights are on at night?"
[769] Captain Sart spat into the spittoon. "Not too clearly, the part under the awning is completely unseen, especially at night, with the fog so thick, and the steering room's light reflecting off the water, it's as dark as the devil's own bottom. You know, the steering room looks like a scoop, with the opening facing the front of the ship."
[770] "So, between 10:45 and 11:40, you didn't see or hear anyone appear on the top deck?"
[771] "Listen here," the captain growled. "Have you ever tried rowing a boat through the fog at night? Sir, you have to focus all your attention on keeping the boat on course. You can't afford to be distracted."
[772] "Very well, I understand," Lain retreated. Bruno frowned and nodded for the crew to leave.
[773] Bruno stood on the chair and shouted, "Now, anyone who personally saw someone fall into the water on the top deck, come forward."
[774] Six people raised their hands, and they hesitated and shuffled before finally emerging. Facing Bruno's relentless questioning, the six individuals appeared uneasy, but when they spoke, their voices harmonized.
[775] "One at a time, one at a time," Bruno shouted, jumping down from the chair and selecting a round, short man with blond hair and a big belly. "You first – what's your name?"
[776] "August Hafmeyer, sir," the little man said nervously. He wore a round hat like a clerk's and a black tie that looked like a rope, his clothes were ragged and stained with oil. "I'm a printer – I'm heading home from work."
[777] "A printer heading home from work," Bruno said, tapping his foot and swaying his body lightly. "Very well, Hafmeyer. When the ship docked, did you see someone fall from the upper deck?"
[778] "Yes, sir, yes," the German man said.
[779] "Where were you at the time?"
[780] "I was in the room on the ship – oh, the cabin, right by the window," the German man licked his thick lips and continued, "The ship was about to dock, heading towards those – uh, those big wooden..."
[781] "Stakes, right?"
[782] "Yes, stakes. That's when I saw something big and black, it looked like – I only had time to glance out the window, too fast to see clearly – like something was falling down from above..."
[783] "That's all you saw?"
[784] "Yes, sir. I shouted, 'Someone fell into the water!' Everyone shouted, it seemed like they all saw..."
[785] "That's enough, Hafmeyer." – the little man sighed in relief and stepped back – "Is that what the rest of you saw?"
[786] The choir sang in unison to agree.
[787] "Did anyone see anything else—like the face of the person who fell, for example?"
[788] No one answered. The six people looked at each other, bewildered.
[789] "Good. Jonas, write down their names, professions, and addresses." Jonas walked among the six people, asking and recording their information with practiced speed. Haffmeyer was the first, and after completing the task, he slipped away into the crowd behind him. The second was a dirty Italian man, wearing a black shiny suit and a black work cap—named Giuseppe Salvatore, the ship's shoe shiner. He said that at the time, he was helping a client with their shoes, facing the window. The third was a shabby old lady, Irish, named Martha Wilson. She said she was the janitor at the Times Square commercial building, on her way home, sitting next to Haffmeyer, and saw the same thing he described. The fourth was a well-dressed large man named Henry Nickerson, wearing a plaid three-piece suit. He said he was a traveling salesman of cheap jewelry, passing through the cabin when the incident occurred. The last two were young women, both company employees, named Mae Cohn and Ruth Tobias. They had gone to see a "wonderful show" on Broadway and were on their way back to their residence in New Jersey. They were sitting next to Haffmeyer and Mrs. Wilson when the incident occurred, and they were getting ready to disembark.
[790] Bruno noticed that none of the six had ever seen the man in the ticket booth uniform—or the red-haired man—on this ferry trip. They all said they had boarded the ferry at 11:30 a.m. from New York, and none of them had gone to the top deck. Mrs. Wilson even claimed that she had never been to the top deck—the voyage was too short—and that the weather was "terrible."
[791] Bruno let the six people return to the passenger group and then asked a few simple questions to the others. There were no clues, no one had seen a red-haired ticket collector, and no one had gone to the top deck. Everyone had boarded the ferry at 11:30 a.m. from New York, and none of them had taken the ferry back and forth.
[792] Bruno, Rain, and DeWitt went back upstairs to the station master's office together. Sam was surrounded by his detectives, sitting in a chair with a scowl on his face, staring at the terrible corpse that was supposedly Charles Wood's. As they entered, Sam stood up quickly, glaring at DeWitt with intensity, but swallowed his words. He crossed his arms behind his back and began pacing in front of the flattened corpse.
[793] "Bruno," Sam said in a low voice, "I want to talk to you privately." Bruno wrinkled his nose and walked over to Sam, and the two began to whisper to each other. Occasionally, Bruno would glance at DeWitt's expression. Finally, he nodded heavily and stepped away, leaning against the table.
[794] Sam's words were heavy, and his already ugly face became even more distorted. He walked straight up to DeWitt: "DeWitt, tell me, when did you board the Mohawk ferry tonight? Which trip did you take?"
[795] DeWitt tensed his thin body, and his thick beard quivered. "Before I answer your question, Chief Sam, tell me what right you have to question my whereabouts?"
[796] "Don't bother us, Mr. DeWitt," Bruno said sternly.
[797] DeWitt blinked his eyes and looked at Rene, but the old actor gave him a neutral expression - neither supportive nor unhelpful. DeWitt shrugged his shoulders and faced Sam again: "Well, I took the 11:30 trip."
[798] "Why are you so late coming home tonight?"
[799] "I stayed at the club tonight, the City Exchange Club. Didn't I tell you that when we met on the ship?"
[800] "Yes, yes, you did. Now, in the ten-minute journey, did you go to the upper deck of the passenger deck?"
[801] DeWitt bit his lip: "Am I in trouble again, Inspector Sam? The answer is no."
[802] "Did you see the ticket agent, Wood?"
[803] "No, the answer is still no."
[804] "If you did meet him, could you identify him?"
[805] "I should be able to, I've seen him on the trolley many times, and I remember him well from the last time Lengstrum was killed. But I swear, I didn't see him tonight."
[806] Sam took out a pack of matches, took one out, and slowly lit a cigarette. "Did you talk to Wood on the tram many times?"
[807] "Dear Detective Sir -" DeWitt seemed amused.
[808] "Yes or no?"
[809] "Of course not."

[946] Fourth Act
[947] Detective Sam's Office
[948] September 10th, Thursday, 10:15 am
[949] In Detective Sam's office at police headquarters, a tall, anxious-looking man sat fidgeting with a magazine, clipping his nails, chewing a cigar, and staring out the window at the dull, gray sky. When the door opened, he jumped up in alarm.
[950] Sam's already unattractive face darkened even further, matching the weather outside. He strode in, hung his hat and coat on the coat rack, and flopped heavily into the swivel chair behind his desk, barely glancing at the large man who had followed him in.
[951] Detective Sam sorted through his mail and dialed an internal phone number, dictating two replies to a male secretary. Only then did he turn his stern gaze to the giant man standing awkwardly in front of him.
[952] "Moore, do you have an explanation for yourself? You might have a lot of work to do before the sun sets today."
[953] Moore stammered, "I – I can explain everything, sir, I – I –"
[954] "Spit it out, Moore. You need to understand that you're speaking for your job right now."
[955] Moore reluctantly said, "I watched DeWitt all day yesterday, just like you told me, and I didn't leave the stock exchange club all night. At 10:10, I saw DeWitt leave and get into a taxi to head to the ferry terminal. I hopped into a taxi and followed him. We got stuck in traffic on 42nd Street, and my car got into a minor collision with another vehicle, so I jumped into another taxi and continued to follow. But I didn't see DeWitt's taxi. I knew he was heading to the ferry terminal, so we kept going down 42nd Street. When we got to the terminal, a ferry had just left, so we had to wait two minutes for the next one. I got on the ferry and went to Weehawken, but I couldn't find DeWitt in the waiting room. I checked the schedule and saw that the last train to Weehawken had just left, and the next one wouldn't arrive until after midnight. I was trying to figure out my next move; I was sure DeWitt took that train to Weehawken, so I jumped on a bus and headed to Weehawken –"
[956] "What a mess, isn't it?" Sam's tone softened, and the attack disappeared. "Go on, Mosher."
[957] Mosher took a deep breath and relaxed. "The bus passed the train, so I waited at the station for the train to arrive, but it was strange that DeWitt wasn't on that train. I had no idea what to do - I thought maybe I had misjudged when the passengers got off the train, or maybe they had lost me when my taxi got into an accident with another vehicle. So, I called the main office to report to you, but the receptionist said you were out on a case, so I stayed put and waited for any further developments, so I went back to DeWitt's place and waited outside his house. DeWitt didn't come home until well after midnight - probably around 3 a.m., in a taxi. Then, Greenberg and O'Hara showed up, telling me there had been another murder at the ferry terminal and the various situations that arose after the crime."
[958] "Okay, okay, go do your job. Now go relieve Greenberg and O'Hara."

[973] "No, he was alone."

[983] Dr. Shilling entered Sam's office, still wearing his hat—everyone assumed he was bald, but no one had ever seen him without it—and his eyes were bloodshot, peering out from behind thick, round glasses; a dirty toothpick stuck between his teeth.
